Second, the provers run  $\mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F)$  to obtain (pk, vk). Third, the provers verify that the given proof for i increments  $(i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$  is valid. Fourth, the provers execute protocol  $\mathcal{P}$  to update the proof by k additional increments and generate  $(z_{i+k}, \Pi_{i+k})$ . Finally, the adversary's real-world view comprises all the inputs and messages sent to the corrupted parties during  $\pi_{\mathsf{zk}}^{f_{\mathcal{G}}}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{P}, \mathcal{V}]$ .

In the ideal world, we define an ideal functionality  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}} = \mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{V}]$  (Fig. 4.2) to formalize the information revealed to the adversary.  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}$  sends to the adversary a bit b indicating whether the proof for i increments  $(i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$  is valid, and if the proof is valid, the functionality also sends the final output  $z_{i+k}$ . Crucially,  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}$  does not reveal intermediate computation values, such as  $z_{\ell}$  for  $\ell \in \{i+1, \ldots, i+k-1\}$ .

We say that the scheme satisfies t-zero-knowledge if  $\pi_{zk}^{fg}$  securely computes  $\mathcal{F}_{zk}$  (Definition 14). This essentially means that the adversary's view of the protocol can be simulated using the ideal functionality.

**Notation:** Let there be n parties, representing the provers. Let  $\mathcal{C} \subseteq [n]$  be the corrupted provers, and let  $\mathcal{H}$  (the honest provers) equal  $[n] \setminus \mathcal{C}$ . Let the number of corrupted parties be  $|\mathcal{C}| \leq t$ . Let  $f_{\mathcal{G}}$  be an ideal functionality that takes input  $1^{\lambda}$ , computes  $pp \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ , and sends pp to all parties in [n].

Figure 4.1: Protocol 
$$\pi_{\mathsf{zk}}^{f_{\mathcal{G}}}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{P}, \mathcal{V}]$$

<span id="page-20-0"></span>**Inputs:** Each prover  $j \in [n]$  has inputs  $(\lambda, F, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W_j)$ .

- 1: The parties invoke  $f_{\mathcal{G}}$  on input  $1^{\lambda}$  to sample pp.
- 2: Each party computes the following functions:

$$(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{vk}) \leftarrow \mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F)$$
  
$$b \leftarrow \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$$

3: The parties execute the protocol  $\mathcal{P}$ :

$$(z_{i+k}, \Pi_{i+k}) \leftarrow \mathcal{P}(\mathsf{pk}, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W)$$

4: Output: The honest provers have no outputs.

{21}------------------------------------------------

Figure 4.2: Ideal Functionality  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{V}]$ 

<span id="page-21-2"></span>**Inputs:** Each prover  $j \in [n]$  has inputs  $(\lambda, F, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W_j)$ .

1. The parties send their inputs to the functionality. The functionality also receives a list of the corrupted parties.

The functionality checks that every party sent matching values of  $(\lambda, F, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$ . If not, the functionality aborts.

The functionality parses the parties' witness fragments  $\{W_j\}_{j\in[n]}$  to compute the incremental witnesses  $\{\vec{\omega}_\ell\}_{\ell\in\{i,\dots,i+k-1\}}$  according to Eqs. (4.1) and (4.2).

- 2. The functionality receives pp from a corrupted party. If there are no corrupted parties, then the functionality samples  $pp \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 3. The functionality computes the following:

$$(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{vk}) \leftarrow \mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F),$$
 
$$b \leftarrow \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i),$$
 
$$\{z_{\ell+1} = F(z_{\ell}, \vec{\omega}_{\ell})\}_{\ell \in \{i, \dots, i+k-1\}}$$

**Output:** The corrupted parties receive b. Additionally, if b = 1, then the corrupted parties receive  $z_{i+k}$ .

<span id="page-21-1"></span>**Definition 14** (t-Zero-Knowledge). For a given value t, a candidate collaborative IVC scheme  $(\mathcal{G}, \mathcal{K}, \mathcal{P}, \mathcal{V})$  satisfies t-zero-knowledge if the protocol  $\pi_{\mathsf{zk}}^{f_{\mathcal{G}}}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{P}, \mathcal{V}]$  (Fig. 4.1) securely computes  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{V}]$  (Fig. 4.2) with abort in the  $f_{\mathcal{G}}$ -hybrid model in the presence of a malicious adversary corrupting at most t parties in [n].

## <span id="page-21-0"></span>4.2 The Relation $\mathcal{R}_F$

In this section we begin to describe our construction of collaborative IVC. Each IVC proof will contain instance-witness pairs proving the correct computation of a particular circuit  $H_F$ . In this section, we define  $H_F$  and the associated relation  $\mathcal{R}_F$ .

**Overview.** The relation circuit  $H_F$  (Fig. 4.3) has several functions, including computing one increment of the computation  $(z' = F(z, \vec{\omega}))$  and verifying the most recent round of folding. To extend the IVC proof by one increment, the prover (1) computes  $H_F$ , which involves computing an additional increment  $z' = F(z, \vec{\omega})$ , (2) generates a proof that  $H_F$  was correctly evaluated, and (3) folds this proof into the running proof.

To explain the design of  $H_F$ , let us first recall Nova's relation circuit, which is similar to  $H_F$ . The circuit below is equivalent to Nova's relation circuit F' ([KST22], construction 3). We have just modified the notation and format to match that of  $H_F$ .

 $F'(\mathsf{vk},\mathsf{Inst},\mathsf{inst},\ell,z_0,z,\vec{\omega},\pi,r,r')\to h'$ 

- 1. If  $\ell = 0$ :
  - (a) Set  $Inst' = inst_{\perp}$ .
  - (b) Check that  $z = z_0$ .
- <span id="page-21-5"></span>2. If  $\ell > 0$ :
  - (a) Check that inst.x =  $\mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell, z_0, z, \mathsf{Inst}; r)$ .
  - (b) Check that inst. $\overline{E} = \text{inst}_{\perp}.\overline{E}$  and inst.u = 1.
  - (c) Compute  $Inst' = NIFS.\mathcal{V}(vk, Inst, inst, \pi)$ .
- <span id="page-21-4"></span><span id="page-21-3"></span>3. Compute  $z' = F(z, \vec{\omega})$ .

{22}------------------------------------------------

- 4. Compute  $\ell' = \ell + 1$ .
- <span id="page-22-0"></span>5. Compute and output  $h' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell', z_0, z', \mathsf{Inst}'; r')$ .

Now we explain the main steps of the circuit. Step 3 computes one increment of F, mapping the state z after  $\ell$  increments to the state z' after  $\ell+1$  increments using witness  $\vec{\omega}$ . Step 2c folds the most recently generated instance inst with the accumulated instance Inst to produce a new accumulated instance Inst'. Additionally, step 5 compresses the output of the circuit using HCom.Commit. This is necessary because the circuit's output is included in each instance of the relation, and without compression, the output would be  $(vk, \ell', z_0, z', Inst')$ , which is longer than the instance Inst'. Finally step 2a takes the commitment inst.x that was output by the previous increment and checks that it opens to the values that we expect.

Second, in the collaborative setting, z is secret-shared among the provers. The provers compute

$$[z] = (z_1, \dots, z_n) = \mathsf{SSS}.\mathsf{share}(\mathbb{F}, z, t)$$

and each prover  $j \in [n]$  holds share  $z_j$ .

To maintain t-zero-knowledge, [z] should not be reconstructed during intermediate rounds. However, it is quite expensive to compute F' without reconstructing z. This is because in step 2a, the line

$$\mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{vk},\ell,z_0,z,\mathsf{Inst};r)$$

hashes z using a cryptographic hash function. Computing the hash function on secret-shared inputs is prohibitively expensive.

Our solution is to have each prover commit to their share of [z] individually, and this operation requires no communication among the provers. Let us rename [z] to the vector  $\mathbf{z}$ :

$$\mathbf{z} = (z_1, \dots, z_n) = \mathsf{SSS.Share}(\mathbb{F}, z, t)$$

<span id="page-22-1"></span>where each prover  $j \in [n]$  holds share  $z_j$ . Then, the provers sample  $\mathbf{r} = (r_1, \dots, r_n) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^n$  and compute:

$$h_0 = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell, z_0, \mathsf{Inst}; 0)$$
  
 $h_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z_j; r_j), \quad \forall j \in [n]$   
 $\mathbf{h} = (h_0, h_1, \dots, h_n)$  (4.3)

with each prover  $j \in [n]$  sampling  $r_j$  and computing  $h_0$  and  $h_j$ .

h represents a commitment to  $(vk, \ell, z_0, z, Inst)$ , using randomness r. To verify the opening of such a commitment,  $H_F$  checks Eq. (4.3) and also checks that

$$z = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z})$$

Third, step 3 of F' also acts on z by computing  $z' = F(z, \vec{\omega})$ . To prove the correct evaluation of the relation circuit, we need to compute the wire values of  $F(z, \vec{\omega})$ . Since z is secret-shared, we will use standard MPC techniques (such as [BOGW88, AL11]) to compute shares of these wire values without reconstructing [z]. The details of this step are beyond the scope of this work. F can be any given function, so it is reasonable to use generic MPC protocols here. Additionally, this step is considered part of witness extension, and it does not count toward the overhead of proof generation. This is standard in the study of collaborative zk-SNARKs, as the cost of computing F is unavoidable.

Fourth,  $H_F$  can be run in two modes. When  $H_F$  is run in increment mode,  $H_F$  behaves analogously to the circuit F' above and computes one increment of the IVC. Next, when  $H_F$  is run in zk mode, it performs two rounds of folding and leaves z unchanged (it sets z' = z). This helps us hide sensitive information in the IVC proofs in order to achieve t-zero-knowledge. Finally, in both modes,  $H_F$  also performs some miscellaneous processing steps: checking commitments, folding two instances, and committing to new values.  $H_F$  is described in Fig. 4.3.

Fifth, step 4 of the relation circuit computes the following value of z':

$$z' = \begin{cases} F(z, \vec{\omega}), & \mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{increment} \\ z, & \mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk} \end{cases}$$

Here we add an optimization, using switchboarding to ensure that when  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$ , the parties don't need to communicate during step 4. When  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$ , the  $F(z, \vec{\omega})$  case of the circuit is unused, but

{23}------------------------------------------------

R1CS still requires the evaluator to compute the wire values of F. Since z will be secret-shared among the parties, there can be a relatively high communication cost to computing secret shares of the wire values of  $F(z, \vec{\omega})$ , and we want to avoid needless communication.

Our solution is inspired by Nebula's switchboarding technique [AS24], although we opt for a notationally simpler solution. Instead of computing  $F(z, \vec{\omega})$ , the parties actually compute:

$$z_{\mathsf{out}} = F(z_{\mathsf{in}}, \vec{\omega}_{\mathsf{in}})$$

When  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{increment}$ , the parties set  $(z_{\mathsf{in}}, \vec{\omega}_{\mathsf{in}}) \leftarrow (z, \vec{\omega})$ , and  $z' \leftarrow z_{\mathsf{out}}$ . This ensures that  $z' = F(z, \vec{\omega})$ . However, when  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$ , the parties set  $(z_{\mathsf{in}}, \vec{\omega}_{\mathsf{in}}) \leftarrow (0, 0)$ . Then the inputs to F are (0, 0), which are known to every party. Each party can compute the wire values of  $F(z_{\mathsf{in}}, \vec{\omega}_{\mathsf{in}})$  without any communication. Then the parties set

$$[z'] = [z]$$

which also requires no communication.

Variables and Notation. We define the relation using the following building blocks:

- Pedersen's commitment scheme Ped.(Gen, Commit) (Section 3.3.1).
- The hash-based commitment scheme HCom.(Gen, Commit) (Section 3.3.2). The public parameters pp simply provide query access to a random oracle, so HCom.Gen and pp will be omitted from our notation. Additionally, note that HCom.Commit can commit to vectors of any length.
- Nova's non-interactive folding scheme NIFS. $(\mathcal{G}, \mathcal{K}, \mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2, \mathcal{V})$  instantiated with Pedersen's commitment scheme (Section 3.5.1).

Next, let  $\mathbb{F}$  be a large field. Let  $n \in \mathbb{N}$  be the number of parties, and let  $t \in \{0\} \cup [n-1]$  be the maximum number of corrupted parties. Let  $\mathcal{C} \subset [n]$  be the corrupted parties, and let  $\mathcal{H} = [n] \setminus \mathcal{C}$  be the honest parties.

Let F be the incremental circuit that is applied many times. Specifically, F is a polynomial-sized circuit that takes a current state z and a witness  $\vec{\omega} = (\omega^1, \dots, \omega^n)$  and outputs a new state z'. Next,  $z_0$  is the initial z-value at the start of the IVC, and  $\ell$  is the number of increments of F that have already been computed.

 $\mathbf{z} = (z_j)_{j \in [n]}$  is a secret-sharing of the current state z.  $\mathbf{h} = (h_j)_{j \in \{0\} \cup [n]}$  is a commitment to  $\mathbf{z}$  and other values, and  $\mathbf{r} = (r_j)_{j \in [n]}$  is the randomness of the commitment. Likewise,  $\mathbf{z}' = (z'_j)_{j \in [n]}$  is a secret-sharing of the new state z',  $\mathbf{h}' = (h'_j)_{j \in \{0\} \cup [n]}$  is a commitment to  $\mathbf{z}'$  and other values, and  $\mathbf{r}' = (r'_j)_{j \in [n]}$  is the randomness of the commitment.

Inst, inst' are three instances of the relation that  $H_F$  may fold together using NIFS. $\mathcal{V}$ .  $\pi$  is the folding proof used to combine (Inst, inst')  $\to$  Inst', and  $\pi'$  is the folding proof used to combine (Inst', inst')  $\to$  Inst''.

 $H_F$  takes the following miscellaneous inputs, in addition to the variables defined above. There are two mode variables mode, mode'  $\in$  {increment, zk}. mode is the mode in which the most recently completed increment of  $H_F$  was computed. mode' is the mode in which the upcoming increment of  $H_F$  should be computed. Next,  $vk_{NIFS}$  is the verification key for the non-interactive folding scheme. Finally,  $inst_{\perp}$  is the trivial instance (defined in Eq. (3.3)).

The Relation Circuit. Figure 4.3 describes  $H_F$ . We have highlighted sections of the circuit based on how their witness fragments will be secret shared. The highlighting can be ignored for now. It will mainly be relevant for the collaborative folding protocol in Section 5.

{24}------------------------------------------------

```
Figure 4.3: The Relation Circuit H_F
 1: Inputs: vk_{NIFS}, mode, mode', \ell, z_0, z, \vec{\omega}, inst_{\perp}, Inst, inst, inst', \pi, \pi', h, z, z', r, r'
 2: If \ell = 0:
          1. \operatorname{Inst}' = \operatorname{inst}_{\perp}.
          2. Check that z=z_0
 3: If \ell > 0:
          1. Check that (mode, mode') \neq (zk, zk).
          2. Check that inst.(\overline{E}, u, x) = (\text{inst}_{\perp}, \overline{E}, 1, \mathbf{h}).
          3. Check that h_0 = \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}},\mathsf{mode},\ell,z_0,\mathsf{inst}_\perp,\mathsf{Inst};0).
         4. For every j \in [n], check that h_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z_j; r_j).
          5. Check that z = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}).
         6. \mathsf{Inst}' = \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{Inst}, \mathsf{inst}, \pi).
 4: Compute z': (z' = F(z, \vec{\omega}) \text{ if mode}' = \text{increment, and } z' = z \text{ if mode}' = zk.)
          1. (z_{\mathsf{in}}, \vec{\omega}_{\mathsf{in}}) = (z, \vec{\omega}) \cdot \mathbb{1}_{\mathsf{mode'} = \mathsf{increment}}
          2. z_{\text{out}} = F(z_{\text{in}}, \vec{\omega}_{\text{in}})
         3. z' = z + (z_{\text{out}} - z) \cdot \mathbb{1}_{\text{mode'} = \text{increment}}
 5: If mode' = zk:
         1. \ell' = \ell.
         2. Inst'' = NIFS.\mathcal{V}(vk_{NIFS}, Inst', inst', \pi').
 6: If mode' = increment:
         1. \ell' = \ell + 1.
         2. Inst'' = Inst'.
 7: h_0' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', \ell', z_0, \mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, \mathsf{Inst}''; 0).
 8: For every j \in [n], compute h'_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z'_j; r'_j).
 9: Check that z' = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')
10: Outputs: \mathbf{h}' = (h'_j)_{j \in \{0\} \cup [n]}
```

**The Relation.** We treat all of the inputs to  $H_F$  as private, and only the output  $\mathbf{h}'$  is public. Next, the relation  $\mathcal{R}_F$  is the committed relaxed R1CS relation (Section 3.4) for the circuit  $H_F$ .

Let the structure  $s = (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{C})$  be the R1CS matrices for proving correct computation of  $H_F$ . Let  $\mathbf{W}$  be a tuple of all the inputs and intermediate wire values of the circuit  $H_F$ , and let  $\mathbf{x} = \mathbf{h}'$ .  $\mathbf{W}$  is part of the witness, and  $\mathbf{x}$  is part of the instance.

**Sub-circuits.** Let us split up  $H_F$  into sub-circuits based on the highlighting in Fig. 4.3. We will also split up **W** accordingly.

<span id="page-24-2"></span>1. Let  $H^{\mathsf{plaintext}}$  be the subcircuit of  $H_F$  that computes:

```
(a) If \ell=0:
\ni. \mathsf{Inst}'=\mathsf{inst}_{\perp}.

(b) If \ell>0:
\ni. \mathsf{Check} that (\mathsf{mode},\mathsf{mode}') \neq (\mathsf{zk},\mathsf{zk}).
\nii. \mathsf{Check} that \mathsf{inst}.(\overline{E},u,\mathsf{x})=(\mathsf{inst}_{\perp}.\overline{E},1,\mathbf{h}).
\niii. \mathsf{Check} that h_0=\mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}},\mathsf{mode},\ell,z_0,\mathsf{inst}_{\perp},\mathsf{Inst};0).
\niv. \mathsf{Inst}'=\mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}},\mathsf{Inst},\mathsf{inst},\pi).

(c) If \mathsf{mode}'=\mathsf{zk}:
\ni. \ell'=\ell.
```

{25}------------------------------------------------

```
ii. Inst′′ = NIFS.V(vkNIFS, Inst′
                                      , inst′
                                            , π′
                                                ).
```

(d) If mode′ = increment:

i. 
$$\ell' = \ell + 1$$
.

ii. 
$$Inst'' = Inst'$$
.

(e) h ′ <sup>0</sup> = HCom.Commit(vkNIFS, mode′ , ℓ′ , z0, inst⊥, Inst′′; 0).

Let Wplaintext comprise the inputs vkNIFS, mode, mode′ , ℓ, z0, inst⊥, Inst, inst, inst′ , π, π′ , h as well as the intermediate wire values of Hplaintext .

- <span id="page-25-2"></span>2. Let Hshared be the subcircuit of H<sup>F</sup> that computes z ′ :
  - (a) (zin, ⃗ωin) = (z, ⃗ω) · 1mode′=increment
  - (b) zout = F(zin, ⃗ωin)
  - (c) z ′ = z + (zout − z) · 1mode′=increment

Let Wshared comprise the inputs (z, ⃗ω) as well as the intermediate wire values of Hshared. Let W<sup>F</sup> be the wire values of the circuit F(zin, ⃗ωin), which is a subset of the entries of Wshared .

- <span id="page-25-3"></span>3. Let Hmixed be the subcircuit of H<sup>F</sup> that computes:
  - (a) If ℓ = 0, check that z = z0.
  - (b) If ℓ > 0, check that z = SSS.open(F, z).
  - (c) Check that z ′ = SSS.open(F, z ′ ).

Let Wmixed comprise the intermediate wire values of Hmixed .

- <span id="page-25-1"></span>4. For each j ∈ [n], let H<sup>j</sup> be the subcircuit of H<sup>F</sup> that computes:
  - (a) Check that h<sup>j</sup> = HCom.Commit(z<sup>j</sup> ; r<sup>j</sup> ).
  - (b) h ′ <sup>j</sup> = HCom.Commit(z ′ j ; r ′ j ).

Let W<sup>j</sup> comprise the inputs z<sup>j</sup> , z′ j , r<sup>j</sup> , r′ j as well as the intermediate wire values of H<sup>j</sup> .

Finally, for each subcircuit label subcircuit ∈ {plaintext,shared, mixed, 1, . . . , n},

- Let Nsubcircuit be the length of Wsubcircuit .
- Let Esubcircuit , Tsubcircuit be the components of E, T that correspond to gates in Hsubcircuit. Let Msubcircuit be the length of Esubcircuit or Tsubcircuit .
- Let Asubcircuit , Bsubcircuit , Csubcircuit be the rows of A, B, C that correspond to gates Hsubcircuit .

## <span id="page-25-0"></span>4.3 Collaborative Folding Functionality

We present an ideal functionality FCFS that supports folding and other operations for the relation R<sup>F</sup> (CFS stands for collaborative folding scheme). The purpose of this functionality is to abstract away all the MPC techniques we use to construct collaborative IVC. Later on, [Section 5](#page-48-0) presents an MPC protocol that securely computes FCFS, but our construction of IVC in [Section 4.4](#page-30-0) is agnostic to the details of the MPC.

Overview. At a high level, FCFS works as follows. It stores three instance-witness pairs (instA,wA), (instB,wB), (inst<sup>C</sup> ,w<sup>C</sup> ) and applies various operations to them. The functionality never outputs wA, wB, or w<sup>C</sup> until Output is called at the end. This keeps the witnesses hidden from the adversary during the majority of the protocol. This will allow us to argue t-zero-knowledge because the witnesses are only revealed after we are sure that they will not leak sensitive information.

The operations (listed below) may read from and write to the functionality's state and interact with external parties. In general, Fold writes its output to position A; Increment and ZK write their outputs to position B; and Rand writes its output to position C. Additionally, Input writes to any of the three positions, and Output reads from any subset of the positions.

{26}------------------------------------------------

- Input [\(Fig. 4.5\)](#page-26-0): Takes an instance-witness pair (inst,w) and stores it in one of the three positions, A, B, or C.
- Fold [\(Fig. 4.6\)](#page-27-0): Folds together two instance-witness pairs selected from positions A, B, and C, and writes the resulting instance-witness pair to position A.
- Increment [\(Fig. 4.7\)](#page-28-0): Performs one increment of the IVC. This entails evaluating H<sup>F</sup> in increment mode and generating an instance-witness pair for this evaluation. Finally, Increment writes the resulting instance-witness pair to position B.
- ZK [\(Fig. 4.8\)](#page-29-0): Performs various operations to ensure that the IVC proof satisfies t-zero-knowledge. This entails evaluating H<sup>F</sup> in zk mode and generating an instance-witness pair for this evaluation. Finally, ZK writes the resulting instance-witness pair to position B.
- Rand [\(Fig. 4.9\)](#page-30-1): Generates a random accepting instance-witness pair, and writes it to position C.
- Output [\(Fig. 4.10\)](#page-30-2): Outputs a subset of the instance-witness pairs stored by the functionality. After Output is invoked, the user cannot perform subsequent operations.

Additionally, we allow the adversary to modify various outputs of the functionality, such as an instance inst or a folding proof π. This models the effect of malicious behavior when the parties reconstruct secret-shared values in the MPC protocol. During reconstruction, the adversary is rushing, meaning that they see the honest parties' shares before they choose their own shares. This allows the adversary to choose the reconstructed value arbitrarily while still learning the value that was supposed to be reconstructed. Our functionality models the rushing attack as follows. Whenever the functionality wants to output a value to the users, they first send the value to the adversary and allow the adversary to modify it. Then they output the modified value to the honest users.

<span id="page-26-1"></span>The Functionality. [Figure 4.4](#page-26-1) presents the functionality FCFS. NIFS is Nova's non-interactive folding scheme [\(Section 3.5.1\)](#page-16-0).

## Figure 4.4: Ideal Functionality FCFS

## 1: Initialization:

- 1. The functionality has an internal state comprising the following variables: (instA, instB, inst<sup>C</sup> ),(wA,wB,w<sup>C</sup> ), pkNIFS, C.
- 2. The functionality takes as input a prover key pkNIFS and a set of corrupted parties C and stores them in the state.
- 3. The rest of the state variables are initialized as follows:

$$(\mathsf{inst}_A, \mathsf{w}_A) = (\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B) = (\mathsf{inst}_C, \mathsf{w}_C) = (\mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{w}_\perp)$$

- 2: Operation: The parties can invoke the functionality on the operations op ∈ {Input, Fold, Increment, ZK, Rand} many times and in any order. They are described in [Figs. 4.5](#page-26-0) to [4.9.](#page-30-1)
- 3: Output: The parties may invoke the operation op = Output (described in [Fig. 4.10\)](#page-30-2), after which the functionality stops responding to future instructions from the parties.

Figure 4.5: Operation Input

<span id="page-26-0"></span>Inputs: The parties supply (inst,w) and a position P ∈ {A, B, C}.

1: Set (inst<sup>P</sup> ,w<sup>P</sup> ) ← (inst,w).

{27}------------------------------------------------

## Figure 4.6: Operation Fold

<span id="page-27-0"></span>Inputs: The parties supply two distinct positions P, Q ∈ {A, B, C}. The functionality reads (inst<sup>P</sup> ,w<sup>P</sup> , instQ,wQ, pkNIFS) from its internal state.

1. Compute

$$(\mathsf{state}, \pi) = \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{P}_1(\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, (\mathsf{inst}_P, \mathsf{w}_P), (\mathsf{inst}_Q, \mathsf{w}_Q)).$$

- 2. Send π to the adversary. If the adversary is malicious, then they respond with π ′ . If the adversary is semi-honest, then set π ′ = π.
- 3. Compute NIFS.P<sup>2</sup> and update the values of (instA,wA) as follows:

$$(\mathsf{inst}_A, \mathsf{w}_A) \leftarrow \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{P}_2(\mathsf{state}, \pi')$$

4. Send (instA, π′ ) to all honest parties, and send inst<sup>A</sup> to the corrupted parties.

{28}------------------------------------------------

#### Figure 4.7: Operation Increment

<span id="page-28-0"></span>Inputs: The user supplies  $(\ell, z_0, \vec{\omega}, \mathsf{Inst}, \mathsf{inst}, \pi)$ . The adversary supplies  $\mathbf{r}'_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathbf{z}'_{\mathcal{C}}$  (the corrupted parties' shares of  $\mathbf{r}', \mathbf{z}'$ ). If  $\ell = 0$ , the adversary also supplies  $[z_0]_{\mathcal{C}}$ . The function reads  $(\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathcal{C}, \mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B)$  from the internal state of  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$ .

- 1: From  $\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$  read the commitment keys  $(\mathsf{pp}_E, \mathsf{pp}_W)$  and  $\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$ . Also compute  $\mathsf{inst}_{\perp}$  (Eq. (3.3)).
- 2: If  $\ell = 0$ , compute:

$$\mathbf{z} = \mathsf{SSS}.\mathsf{share}(\mathbb{F}, z_0, [z_0]_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathcal{C}, t)$$
 
$$(\mathsf{mode}, z, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}) = (\mathsf{increment}, z_0, \mathbf{0}^{n+1}, \mathbf{0}^n)$$

3: Otherwise (if  $\ell \geq 1$ ), read from (inst<sub>B</sub>, w<sub>B</sub>), the values (inst<sub>B</sub>, w<sub>B</sub>).(mode', z',  $\mathbf{z}'$ ,  $\mathbf{h}'$ ,  $\mathbf{r}'$ ) and rename them:

$$(\mathsf{mode}, z, \mathbf{z}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}) \leftarrow (\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B).(\mathsf{mode}', z', \mathbf{z}', \mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}').$$

4: Compute

$$z' = F(z, \vec{\omega})$$
  
 $\mathbf{z}' = \mathsf{SSS.share}(\mathbb{F}, z', \mathbf{z}'_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathcal{C}, t)$ 

- 5: Sample  $r_{\mathbf{W}} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}, \mathbf{r}_{\mathcal{H}}' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{|\mathcal{H}|}$  independently.
- 6: Let

$$\begin{aligned} \mathsf{mode}' &= \mathsf{increment} \\ (\mathsf{inst}', \pi') &= (\mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, 0) \\ \mathbf{r}' &= (\mathbf{r}_{\mathcal{C}}', \mathbf{r}_{\mathcal{H}}') \end{aligned}$$

7: Compute the wire values of the following evaluation of  $H_F$ :

$$H_F(\mathsf{vk}_\mathsf{NIFS},\mathsf{mode},\mathsf{mode}',\ell,z_0,z,\vec{\omega},\mathsf{inst}_\perp,\mathsf{Inst},\mathsf{inst}',\pi,\pi',\mathbf{h},\mathbf{z},\mathbf{z}',\mathbf{r},\mathbf{r}')$$

Let x = h' be the output of  $H_F$ , and let **W** comprise all inputs and intermediate wire values of  $H_F$ .

8: Compute the following:

$$\begin{split} (\mathbf{E}, r_{\mathbf{E}}, u) &= (\mathbf{0}^{M}, 0, 1) \\ \overline{E} &= \mathsf{Ped.Commit}(\mathsf{pp}_{E}, \mathbf{E}; r_{\mathbf{E}}), \\ \overline{W} &= \mathsf{Ped.Commit}(\mathsf{pp}_{W}, \mathbf{W}; r_{\mathbf{W}}). \end{split}$$

- 9: Set inst =  $(\overline{E}, u, \overline{W}, x)$ , and  $w = (\mathbf{E}, r_{\mathbf{E}}, \mathbf{W}, r_{\mathbf{W}})$ .
- 10: Send inst to the adversary. If the adversary is malicious, then they respond with inst'. If the adversary is semi-honest, then set inst' = inst.
- 11: Set  $(\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B) \leftarrow (\mathsf{inst}', \mathsf{w})$ , and send  $\mathsf{inst}'$  to all honest parties.

{29}------------------------------------------------

#### Figure 4.8: Operation ZK

<span id="page-29-0"></span>**Inputs:** The user supplies  $(\ell, z_0, \mathsf{Inst}, \mathsf{inst}', \pi, \pi')$ . The adversary supplies  $\mathbf{r}'_{\mathcal{C}}$  (the corrupted parties' shares of  $\mathbf{r}'$ ). If  $\ell = 0$ , the adversary also supplies  $[z_0]_{\mathcal{C}}$ . The function reads  $(\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathcal{C}, \mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B)$  from the internal state of  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$ .

- 1: From  $\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$  read the commitment keys  $(\mathsf{pp}_E, \mathsf{pp}_W)$  and  $\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$ . Also compute  $\mathsf{inst}_{\perp}$  (Eq. (3.3)).
- 2: If  $\ell = 0$ , compute:

$$\mathbf{z} = \mathsf{SSS}.\mathsf{share}(\mathbb{F}, z_0, [z_0]_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathcal{C}, t)$$

$$(\mathsf{mode}, z, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}) = (\mathsf{increment}, z_0, \mathbf{0}^{n+1}, \mathbf{0}^n)$$

3: Otherwise (if  $\ell \geq 1$ ), read from (inst<sub>B</sub>, w<sub>B</sub>), the values (inst<sub>B</sub>, w<sub>B</sub>).(mode', z',  $\mathbf{z}'$ ,  $\mathbf{h}'$ ,  $\mathbf{r}'$ ) and rename them:

$$(\mathsf{mode}, z, \mathbf{z}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}) \leftarrow (\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B).(\mathsf{mode}', z', \mathbf{z}', \mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}').$$

4: Set

$$(z',\mathbf{z}')=(z,\mathbf{z})$$

- 5: Sample  $r_{\mathbf{W}} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}, \mathbf{r}_{\mathcal{H}}' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{|\mathcal{H}|}$  independently.
- 6: Let

$$\begin{aligned} \mathsf{mode}' &= \mathsf{zk} \ & \vec{\omega} &= \mathbf{0} \ & \mathbf{r}' &= (\mathbf{r}_{\mathcal{C}}', \mathbf{r}_{\mathcal{H}}') \end{aligned}$$

7: Compute the wire values of the following evaluation of  $H_F$ :

$$H_F(\mathsf{vk}_\mathsf{NIFS},\mathsf{mode},\mathsf{mode}',\ell,z_0,z,\vec{\omega},\mathsf{inst}_\perp,\mathsf{Inst},\mathsf{inst}',\pi,\pi',\mathbf{h},\mathbf{z},\mathbf{z}',\mathbf{r},\mathbf{r}')$$

Let  $x = \mathbf{h}'$  be the output of  $H_F$ , and let **W** comprise all inputs and intermediate wire values of  $H_F$ .

8: Compute the following commitments:

$$\begin{split} (\mathbf{E}, r_{\mathbf{E}}, u) &= (\mathbf{0}^{M}, 0, 1) \\ \overline{E} &= \mathsf{Ped.Commit}(\mathsf{pp}_{E}, \mathbf{E}; r_{\mathbf{E}}), \\ \overline{W} &= \mathsf{Ped.Commit}(\mathsf{pp}_{W}, \mathbf{W}; r_{\mathbf{W}}). \end{split}$$

- 9: Set inst =  $(\overline{E}, u, \overline{W}, x)$ , and  $w = (\mathbf{E}, r_{\mathbf{E}}, \mathbf{W}, r_{\mathbf{W}})$ .
- 10: Send inst to the adversary. If the adversary is malicious, then they respond with inst'. If the adversary is semi-honest, then set inst' = inst.
- 11: Set  $(\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B) \leftarrow (\mathsf{inst}', \mathsf{w})$ , and send  $\mathsf{inst}'$  to all honest parties.

{30}------------------------------------------------

#### Figure 4.9: Operation Rand

<span id="page-30-1"></span>Inputs: The corrupted parties supply  $\mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{plaintext}}$  (defined in step 1) and  $(\mathbf{W}^{j})_{j \in \mathcal{C}}$  (defined in step 4). The functionality also reads  $\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$  from the internal state of  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$ .

- 1: From  $\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$ , read the commitment keys  $(\mathsf{pp}_E, \mathsf{pp}_W)$ , the R1CS structure  $(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{C})$ , and the parameters (L, M, N).
- 2: Sample the rest of **W**.
  - 1. If  $|\mathcal{C}| = 0$  (there are no corrupted provers), then sample  $\mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{plaintext}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{N^{\mathsf{plaintext}}}$ .
  - 2. Sample  $\mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{shared}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{N^{\mathsf{shared}}}, \, \mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{mixed}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{N^{\mathsf{mixed}}}, \, \text{and for each } j \in \mathcal{H}, \, \text{sample } \mathbf{W}^{j} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{N^{j}}.$
  - 3. Let

$$\mathbf{W} = \left(\mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{plaintext}}, \mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{shared}}, \mathbf{W}^{\mathsf{mixed}}, (\mathbf{W}^{j})_{j \in [n]} \right)$$

- 3: Sample  $(r_{\mathbf{W}}, r_{\mathbf{E}}, u, \mathsf{x}) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{F}^{1+1+1+L}$ .
- 4: Compute the following values:

$$\begin{aligned} \mathbf{Z} &= \left( \mathbf{W}, \mathbf{x}, u \right), \ \mathbf{E} &= \left( \mathbf{A} \cdot \mathbf{Z} \right) \circ \left( \mathbf{B} \cdot \mathbf{Z} \right) - u \cdot \left( \mathbf{C} \cdot \mathbf{Z} \right), \ \overline{E} &= \mathsf{Ped.Commit}(\mathsf{pp}_E, \mathbf{E}; r_{\mathbf{E}}), \ \overline{W} &= \mathsf{Ped.Commit}(\mathsf{pp}_W, \mathbf{W}; r_{\mathbf{W}}). \end{aligned}$$

- 5: Set inst  $= (\overline{E}, u, \overline{W}, x), w = (\mathbf{E}, r_{\mathbf{E}}, \mathbf{W}, r_{\mathbf{W}}).$
- 6: Send inst to the adversary. If the adversary is malicious, then they respond with inst'. If the adversary is semi-honest, then set inst' = inst.
- 7: Set  $(inst_C, w_C) \leftarrow (inst', w)$ , and send inst' to all honest parties.

#### Figure 4.10: Operation Output

<span id="page-30-2"></span>**Inputs:** The parties supply a list of positions  $L \subseteq \{A, B, C\}$  to output. For each  $P \in L$ :

- 1. Send  $(inst_P, w_P)$  to the adversary.
- 2. If the adversary is malicious, then they respond with  $(\mathsf{inst}_P', \mathsf{w}_P')$ . If the adversary is semi-honest, then set  $(\mathsf{inst}_P', \mathsf{w}_P') = (\mathsf{inst}_P, \mathsf{w}_P)$ .
- 3. Send  $(inst'_P, w'_P)$  to the honest parties.

## <span id="page-30-0"></span>4.4 Construction of Collaborative IVC

Here we present our collaborative IVC construction in the  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$  hybrid model.

- $\mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ :
  - 1. Sample  $pp = pp_{NIFS} \leftarrow NIFS.\mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ , and output pp.
- $\mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F)$ :
  - 1. Compute  $s = (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{C})$ , the R1CS structure for the relation  $\mathcal{R}_F$  (Section 4.2).
  - 2. Compute  $(pk_{NIFS}, vk_{NIFS}) = NIFS.\mathcal{K}(pp, s)$ .
  - 3. Compute  $pk = (pp, F, pk_{NIFS}, vk_{NIFS})$ , and  $vk = (pp, F, vk_{NIFS})$ .
  - 4. Output (pk, vk).
- $\mathcal{P}(\mathsf{pk}, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W)$ :

{31}------------------------------------------------

- <span id="page-31-0"></span>1. Parse the inputs:
  - (a) Parse pk as  $(pp, F, pk_{NIFS}, vk_{NIFS})$ . Set  $vk = (pp, F, vk_{NIFS})$ .
  - (b) Parse  $W = (\vec{\omega}_{\ell})_{\ell \in \{i,\dots,i+k-1\}} = (\omega_{\ell}^{j})_{j \in [n], \ell \in \{i,\dots,i+k-1\}}$ .
  - (c) If  $i \geq 1$ , then parse  $\Pi_i$  as  $((\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i), (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i))$ . Otherwise (if i = 0), then set  $(\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i) = (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i) = (\mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{w}_\perp)$ .
- <span id="page-31-2"></span>2. Compute  $b = \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$ . If  $\mathcal{V}$  rejects (b = 0), then output  $\bot$  and halt. Otherwise, continue.
- <span id="page-31-3"></span>3. If k = 0, then output  $z_{i+k} = z_i$  and  $\Pi_{i+k} = \Pi_i$ , and halt. Otherwise continue.
- <span id="page-31-1"></span>4. Initialize  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$ :
  - (a) Initialize  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$  with inputs  $\mathsf{pk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}$  and  $\mathcal{C}$  (the corrupted parties).
  - (b) The parties call Input (Fig. 4.5) to write the pair (Inst<sub>i</sub>,  $W_i$ ) to position A.
  - (c) The parties call Input to write the pair  $(inst_i, w_i)$  to position B.
- <span id="page-31-6"></span><span id="page-31-5"></span><span id="page-31-4"></span>5. Compute k increments of the proof. For each  $\ell \in \{i, \ldots, i+k-1\}$ :
  - (a) The parties call Fold (Fig. 4.6) to fold positions A and B together. The result (Inst<sub> $\ell+1$ </sub>, W<sub> $\ell+1$ </sub>) is written to position A, and the parties receive (Inst<sub> $\ell+1$ </sub>,  $\pi_{\ell}$ ).
  - (b) The parties call Increment (Fig. 4.7) with inputs

$$(\ell, z_0, \vec{\omega}_\ell, \mathsf{Inst}_\ell, \mathsf{inst}_\ell, \pi_\ell)$$

The result (inst<sub> $\ell+1$ </sub>, w<sub> $\ell+1$ </sub>) is written to position B, and the parties receive inst<sub> $\ell+1$ </sub>.

- <span id="page-31-10"></span><span id="page-31-9"></span><span id="page-31-8"></span><span id="page-31-7"></span>6. Add zero-knowledge:
  - (a) The parties call Fold to fold positions A and B together. The result (Inst', W') is written to position A, and the parties receive (Inst',  $\pi$ ).
  - (b) The parties call Rand (Fig. 4.9). Then the result (inst', w') is written to position C, and the parties receive inst'.
  - (c) The parties call Fold to fold positions A and C together. The result (Inst", W") is written to position A, and the parties receive (Inst",  $\pi$ ').
  - (d) The parties call ZK (Fig. 4.8) with inputs

$$(i+k, z_0, \mathsf{Inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{inst}', \pi, \pi')$$

The result (inst", w") is written to position B, and the parties receive inst".

- <span id="page-31-12"></span><span id="page-31-11"></span>7. Output:
  - (a) The parties call Output (Fig. 4.10) for positions A and B, and they receive (Inst", W", inst", w").
  - (b) The parties read the value z from w'' and define the following variables:

$$z_{i+k} = \mathbf{w}''.z$$
 
$$\Pi_{i+k} = \big( (\mathsf{Inst}'', \mathbf{W}''), (\mathsf{inst}'', \mathbf{w}'') \big)$$

- (c) Output  $(z_{i+k}, \Pi_{i+k})$ .
- $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$ :
  - 1. If i = 0, then check that  $z_0 = z_i$ .
  - 2. If  $i \ge 1$ :
    - (a) Parse vk as (pp, F, vk<sub>NIFS</sub>). Parse  $\Pi_i$  as ((Inst, W), (inst, w)). From (inst, w) read the values (mode',  $\mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}', \mathbf{z}'$ ).
    - (b) Check that

$$h_0' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', i, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, \mathsf{Inst}; 0)$$

<span id="page-31-13"></span>and for every  $j \in [n]$ , check that

$$h'_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z'_j; r'_j).$$

- <span id="page-31-14"></span>(c) Check that  $z_i = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ .
- (d) Check that inst. $\overline{E} = \text{inst}_{\perp}.\overline{E}$  and inst.u = 1.
- (e) Check that  $(Inst, W) \in \mathcal{R}_F$  and  $(inst, w) \in \mathcal{R}_F$  using the checks in Eq. (3.2).
- <span id="page-31-16"></span><span id="page-31-15"></span>3. If all checks pass, then output 1 (accept). Otherwise, output 0 (reject).

{32}------------------------------------------------

The following theorem says that the construction above is a collaborative IVC scheme, and this holds when  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$  is instantiated by a real-world protocol.

<span id="page-32-2"></span>Theorem 15 (Collaborative IVC). Let  $t < \frac{n}{2}$ . In the collaborative IVC construction (Section 4.4), let  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  be replaced with any protocol  $\pi_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  that securely computes  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  with abort in the presence of a malicious adversary controlling  $\leq t$  parties. Then the resulting protocol satisfies incremental completeness, adaptive knowledge soundness, succinctness (Definition 12), and t-zero-knowledge (Definition 14).

*Proof.* The proof is given in Section 4.5, where we prove incremental completeness (Lemma 16), adaptive knowledge soundness (Lemma 22), t-zero-knowledge (Lemma 23), and succinctness (Lemma 29).

## <span id="page-32-0"></span>4.5 Analysis of CIVC Construction

Here we prove that our collaborative IVC construction (Section 4.4) satisfies the properties listed in Definition 13: incremental completeness (Lemma 16), adaptive knowledge soundness (Lemma 22), t-zero-knowledge (Lemma 23), and succinctness (Lemma 29). We also analyze the communication complexity of the protocol in Lemma 30.

### <span id="page-32-1"></span>4.5.1 Incremental Completeness

<span id="page-32-3"></span>Lemma 16 (Incremental Completeness). The collaborative IVC construction in Section 4.4 satisfies incremental completeness (Definition 12).

*Proof.* In the completeness experiment we assume that all parties are honest, and in this setting,  $\pi_{CFS}$  correctly computes  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$ . Then it suffices to prove completeness in the  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$ -hybrid model, and completeness will hold for the real-world protocol as well.

Let  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$  and let F be a polynomial-sized circuit.

**Base Case.** Let  $z_0$  be an initial state. Let pp be in the support of  $\mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ , and set the following variables:

$$\begin{split} (\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{vk}) &\leftarrow \mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F) \\ \widetilde{z_0}, \Pi_0 &\leftarrow \mathcal{P}(\mathsf{pk}, 0, 0, z_0, z_0, \bot, \bot) \\ b &\leftarrow \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, 0, z_0, \widetilde{z_0}, \Pi_0). \end{split}$$

We will show that b=1 and  $\widetilde{z_0}=z_0$  with probability 1.  $\mathcal{P}(\mathsf{pk},0,0,z_0,z_0,\bot,\bot)$  acts as follows. First  $\mathcal{P}$  computes  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk},i,z_0,z_i,\Pi_i)$ , with  $i=0,\,z_i=z_0,\,\Pi_i=\bot$ .  $\mathcal{V}$  outputs 1 on these inputs. Second, since  $k=0,\,\mathcal{P}$  outputs  $\widetilde{z_0}=z_0$  and  $\Pi_0=\bot$ .

Next,  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, 0, z_0, \widetilde{z_0}, \Pi_0)$  acts as follows. Since i = 0 and  $z_0 = \widetilde{z_0}$ ,  $\mathcal{V}$  outputs b = 1. In summary, the base case is satisfied because  $\widetilde{z_0} = z_0$  and b = 1 with probability 1.

Inductive Case. Let  $i \geq 0, k \geq 1$ ; let  $z_0, z_i$  be states; let  $\Pi_i$  be a proof for the first i increments; let  $W = (\vec{\omega}_i, \dots, \vec{\omega}_{i+k-1})$  be witnesses for the next k increments of F. For every  $\ell \in \{i, \dots, i+k-1\}$ , let  $\vec{\omega}_\ell = (\omega_\ell^1, \dots, \omega_\ell^n)$ . Let pp be in the support of  $\mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ , and set the following variables:

$$\begin{split} (\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{vk}) &\leftarrow \mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp},F) \\ b_i &\leftarrow \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk},i,z_0,z_i,\Pi_i) \\ \{z_{\ell+1} &= F(z_\ell,\vec{\omega}_\ell)\}_{\ell \in \{i,\dots,i+k-1\}} \\ \widetilde{z_{i+k}}, \Pi_{i+k} &\leftarrow \mathcal{P}\left(\mathsf{pk},i,k,z_0,z_i,\Pi_i,W\right) \\ b_{i+k} &\leftarrow \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk},i+k,z_0,\widetilde{z_{i+k}},\Pi_{i+k}). \end{split}$$

We consider the case where  $b_i = 1$ , and show that in this case  $b_{i+k} = 1$  and  $\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = z_{i+k}$ . To do so, let us step through the execution of  $\mathcal{P}(\mathsf{pk}, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W)$ .

Steps 1 - 4 of  $\mathcal{P}$  (initialization): At the end of step 4,  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$  stores in  $(inst_A, w_A), (inst_B, w_B)$  two accepting instance-witness pairs that represent a valid proof of i increments.

In step 1, if i = 0, then  $\mathcal{P}$  sets  $(\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i) = (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i) = (\mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{w}_\perp)$ , which is in  $\mathcal{R}_F$ . Otherwise (if  $i \geq 1$ ),  $\mathcal{P}$  parses

$$\Pi_i = ((\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i), (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i)).$$

{33}------------------------------------------------

These two instance-witness pairs are in  $\mathcal{R}_F$ . This fact is checked by  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$ , and all checks pass because we assumed  $b_i = 1$ .

In step 2,  $\mathcal{V}$  accepts because  $b_i = 1$ , so  $\mathcal{P}$  continues on. In step 3,  $k \neq 0$ , so  $\mathcal{P}$  continues as well. In step 4,  $\mathcal{P}$  calls Input to set

$$((\mathsf{inst}_A, \mathsf{w}_A), (\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B)) = ((\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i), (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i))$$

If  $i \geq 1$ , then the values  $(\mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}', \mathbf{z}')$  in  $(\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i)$  satisfy

$$h'_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z'_j; r'_j) \quad \forall j \in [n], \text{ and}$$
  
 $z_i = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ 

This is because  $V(vk, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i) = 1$ , and V explicitly checks these conditions.

Step 5 of  $\mathcal{P}$  (computing k increments): We will show that each iteration of step 5 extends the IVC proof stored in  $((\mathsf{inst}_A, \mathsf{w}_A), (\mathsf{inst}_B, \mathsf{w}_B))$  by one increment.

For each  $\ell \in \{i, \ldots, i+k-1\}$ , let

$$\Pi'_{\ell+1} = ((\mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{W}_{\ell+1}), (\mathsf{inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}))$$

Note that  $((Inst_{\ell+1}, W_{\ell+1}), (inst_{\ell+1}, w_{\ell+1}))$  are stored in  $((inst_A, w_A), (inst_B, w_B))$  at the end of the  $(\ell+1-i)$ -th iteration of step 5. We will show that  $\Pi'_{\ell+1}$  represents a valid proof of  $\ell+1$  increments.

<span id="page-33-0"></span>Claim 17. For each increment  $\ell \in \{i, \ldots, i+k-1\}$ ,

$$1 = \mathcal{V}\left(\mathsf{vk}, \ell + 1, z_0, z_{\ell+1}, \Pi'_{\ell+1}\right), \text{ and } z_{\ell+1} = \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}.z'$$

*Proof.* Let us prove this claim for the first iteration  $(\ell = i)$ . The proof for the later iterations follows essentially the same argument.

First, when  $\ell = i$ , we have that  $(\mathsf{Inst}_\ell, \mathsf{W}_\ell) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ ,  $(\mathsf{inst}_\ell, \mathsf{w}_\ell) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ . If i = 0, then  $\mathcal{P}$  sets  $(\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i) = (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i) = (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ . If  $i \geq 1$ , then  $\mathcal{V}$  in step 2 ensures that  $(\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i) \in \mathcal{R}_F$  and  $(\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ .

Second, in step 5a, Fold uses NIFS. $\mathcal{P}_1$ , NIFS. $\mathcal{P}_2$  to fold  $(\mathsf{Inst}_\ell, \mathsf{W}_\ell)$  and  $(\mathsf{inst}_\ell, \mathsf{w}_\ell)$  together to produce  $(\mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{W}_{\ell+1})$ . We have that  $(\mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{W}_{\ell+1}) \in \mathcal{R}_F$  by the completeness of the folding scheme NIFS and the fact that  $(\mathsf{Inst}_\ell, \mathsf{W}_\ell)$ ,  $(\mathsf{inst}_\ell, \mathsf{w}_\ell) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ .

Third, in step 5b, the Increment function sets  $z=z_{\ell}$ . If  $\ell=0$ , then Increment sets  $z=z_0=z_{\ell}$ . If  $\ell\geq 1$ , then Increment sets  $z=\mathsf{w}_B.z'=\mathsf{w}_{\ell}.z'$ . We know that  $\mathcal V$  accepts the proof of  $\ell$  increments:

$$\mathcal{V}\left[\mathsf{vk},\ell,z_0,z_\ell,((\mathsf{Inst}_\ell,\mathsf{W}_\ell),(\mathsf{inst}_\ell,\mathsf{w}_\ell))\right]=1.$$

The checks of  $\mathcal{V}$  (and  $H_F$ ) ensure that

$$z_{\ell} = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathsf{w}_{\ell}.\mathbf{z}') = \mathsf{w}_{\ell}.z'.$$

Therefore, Increment sets  $z = z_{\ell}$ .

Fourth, Increment computes

$$z' = F(z_{\ell}, \vec{\omega}_{\ell}) = z_{\ell+1}$$
  
 $\mathbf{z}' = \mathsf{SSS.share}(\mathbb{F}, z', \mathbf{z}'_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathcal{C}, t)$ 

Additionally, Increment computes the wire values of  $H_F$ , which entails computing:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{Inst}'' &= \mathsf{Inst}' = \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk_{NIFS}}, \mathsf{Inst}, \mathsf{inst}, \pi) \\ &= \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk_{NIFS}}, \mathsf{Inst}_\ell, \mathsf{inst}_\ell, \pi_\ell) = \mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1} \\ h_0' &= \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{vk_{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', \ell', z_0, \mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{Inst}''; 0) \\ &= \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{vk_{NIFS}}, \mathsf{increment}, \ell+1, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}; 0) \\ h_j' &= \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(z_j'; r_j'), \quad \forall j \in [n] \end{split}$$

By the properties of the underlying folding scheme NIFS, NIFS. $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}},\mathsf{Inst}_\ell,\mathsf{inst}_\ell,\pi_\ell) = \mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}$ , which was computed by the NIFS prover in step 5a. Additionally, the wire values of  $H_F$  pass all the checks of  $H_F$ , which are listed below:

{34}------------------------------------------------

- 1. If  $\ell = 0$ , then check that  $z = z_0$ . This check passes because we argued above that  $z = z_{\ell}$ .
- 2. If  $\ell > 0$ , then check that (mode, mode')  $\neq$  (zk, zk). This check passes because mode' = increment.
- 3. If  $\ell > 0$ , then check that

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{inst}_\ell.(\overline{E},u,\mathsf{x}) &= (\mathsf{inst}_\perp.\overline{E},1,\mathbf{h}) \\ h_0 &= \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}},\mathsf{mode},\ell,z_0,\mathsf{inst}_\perp,\mathsf{Inst}_\ell;0) \\ h_j &= \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(z_j;r_j), \quad \forall j \in [n] \end{split}$$

These checks pass because  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell, z_0, z_\ell, \Pi'_\ell) = 1$ , and  $\mathcal{V}$  checks these conditions.

- 4. If  $\ell > 0$ , then check that  $z = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z})$ . This check passes because  $z = z_{\ell}$ , as we argued above. Additionally,  $\mathbf{z} = \mathsf{w}_{\ell}.\mathbf{z}'$ , and  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell, z_0, z_{\ell}, \Pi'_{\ell}) = 1$  ensures that  $\mathsf{w}_{\ell}.\mathbf{z}'$  is a sharing of  $z_{\ell}$ . Therefore,  $\mathbf{z}$  is a sharing of z.
- 5. Check that  $z' = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ . This check passes because Increment computes  $\mathbf{z}' = SSS.share(\mathbb{F}, z', \mathbf{z}'_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathcal{C}, t)$ .

Fifth, Increment writes the above values of  $(z', \mathbf{z}', \mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}')$  and the wire values of  $H_F$  into  $(\mathsf{inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1})$ . From the argument above, we have that  $\mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}.z' = z_{\ell+1}$ . Additionally,  $(\mathsf{inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}) \in \mathcal{R}_F$  because  $\mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}$  contains satisfying wire values for  $H_F$ .

Sixth, we claim that  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell+1, z_0, z_{\ell+1}, \Pi'_{\ell+1}) = 1$ . Since  $\ell+1 \geq 1$ ,  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell+1, z_0, z_{\ell+1}, \Pi'_{\ell+1})$  reads  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{increment}$  and  $(\mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}', \mathbf{z}')$  from  $(\mathsf{inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1})$  and makes the following checks:

1. Check that

$$\begin{split} h_0' &= \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', \ell+1, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}; 0) \\ h_j' &= \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z_j'; r_j'), \quad \forall j \in [n]. \end{split}$$

We argued above that Increment computes  $(\mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}', \mathbf{z}')$  to satisfy this check.

- 2. Check that  $z_{\ell+1} = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ . This check passes because  $z_{\ell+1} = \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}.z'$ , and Increment chooses  $\mathbf{z}'$  to be a sharing of  $\mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}.z'$ . Therefore,  $z_{\ell+1} = \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}.z' = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ .
- 3. Check that  $\operatorname{inst}_{\ell+1}.\overline{E} = \operatorname{inst}_{\perp}.\overline{E}$  and  $\operatorname{inst}_{\ell+1}.u = 1$ . This check passes because Increment chooses  $\operatorname{inst}_{\ell+1}.\overline{E} = \operatorname{Ped.Commit}(\operatorname{pp}_E, \mathbf{0}^M; 0) = \operatorname{inst}_{\perp}.\overline{E}$  and  $\operatorname{inst}_{\ell+1}.u = 1$ .
- 4. Check that  $(\mathsf{Inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{W}_{\ell+1}) \in \mathcal{R}_F$  and  $(\mathsf{inst}_{\ell+1}, \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ . We argued above that this check passes. In summary, we have shown that  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, \ell+1, z_0, z_{\ell+1}, \Pi'_{\ell+1}) = 1$  and  $z_{\ell+1} = \mathsf{w}_{\ell+1}.z'$ .

Step 6 of  $\mathcal{P}$  (zero-knowledge layer): We will show that step 6 computes instance-witness pairs  $\Pi_{i+k} = ((\mathsf{Inst''}, \mathsf{W''}), (\mathsf{inst''}, \mathsf{w''}))$  that are in  $\mathcal{R}_F$ .

Claim 18. 
$$(Inst'', W'') \in \mathcal{R}_F$$

*Proof.* We argued above that  $(Inst_{i+k}, W_{i+k})$ ,  $(inst_{i+k}, w_{i+k}) \in \mathcal{R}_F$ . Second, (Inst', W') is the result of folding  $(Inst_{i+k}, W_{i+k})$  and  $(inst_{i+k}, w_{i+k})$  in step 6a, so  $(Inst', W') \in \mathcal{R}_F$  by the correctness of the folding scheme. Third  $(inst', w') \in \mathcal{R}_F$ . (inst', w') is the result of calling Rand in step 6b, and Rand (Fig. 4.9) always outputs values that satisfy the conditions of  $\mathcal{R}_F$  (Eq. (3.2)). Fourth (Inst'', W'') is the result of folding (Inst', W') and (inst', w') in step 6c, so  $(Inst'', W'') \in \mathcal{R}_F$  by the correctness of the folding scheme. □

Claim 19.  $(inst'', w'') \in \mathcal{R}_F$ 

*Proof.* (inst", w") is computed in step 6d by calling ZK on inputs

$$(i+k, z_0, \mathsf{Inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{inst}', \pi, \pi'),$$

where  $\pi$  and  $\pi'$  are the proofs used to generate Inst' and Inst' respectively. Then, ZK sets

$$(z, \mathbf{z}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}) \leftarrow (\mathsf{inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{w}_{i+k}).(z', \mathbf{z}', \mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}')$$

{35}------------------------------------------------

and computes the wire values of  $H_F$  on the inputs

 $(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}},\mathsf{mode} = \mathsf{increment},\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}, i+k, z_0, z, \vec{\omega} = \mathbf{0}, \mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{Inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{inst}', \pi, \pi', \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{z}, \mathbf{z}, \mathbf{r}, \mathbf{r}')$ 

where  $\mathbf{r}'$  is freshly sampled randomness. Then, by the satisfiability of  $\mathsf{inst}_{i+k}$ , we have that all the checks of  $H_F$  pass:

- 1. We have that  $(mode = increment, mode' = zk) \neq (zk, zk)$ .
- 2. By construction of Increment, we have that  $\operatorname{inst}_{i+k}.(\overline{E}, u, \mathsf{x}) = (\operatorname{inst}_{\perp}.\overline{E}, 1, \mathbf{h})$
- 3. By construction of  $H_F$ , Increment, and Fold, we have that

$$h_0 = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{increment}, i + k, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, \mathsf{Inst}_{i+k}; 0)$$

- 4. By the construction of  $H_F$ , we have that  $h_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z_j; r_j)$  for every  $j \in [n]$ .
- 5. By construction of  $H_F$  and Increment, we have that  $z = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z})$ .
- 6. Because  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$  we have that z' = z. Moreover, by the way that  $\mathsf{ZK}$  chooses the input to  $H_F$ , we have that  $\mathsf{z}' = \mathsf{z}$ . Therefore, we have that  $z' = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathsf{z}')$ .

As such, we have that ZK can indeed compute satisfying wire values and as such we have that  $(inst'', w'') \in \mathcal{R}_F$ .

Step 7 of  $\mathcal{P}$  (output): We will show that the final output  $(\widetilde{z_{i+k}}, \Pi_{i+k})$  is accepted by  $\mathcal{V}$  and that  $\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = z_{i+k}$ . In step 7,  $\mathcal{P}$  outputs

$$\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = w''.z$$

$$\Pi_{i+k} = ((Inst'', W''), (inst'', w''))$$

Claim 20.  $V(vk, i + k, z_0, \widetilde{z_{i+k}}, \Pi_{i+k}) = 1.$ 

*Proof.* First, when ZK computes inst", it provides  $H_F$  the instances  $Inst_{i+k}$ ,  $inst_{i+k}$ , inst', as input. Next,  $H_F$  sets  $\ell' = \ell$  because mode' = zk. Additionally,  $H_F$  computes

$$Inst' = \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{Inst}_{i+k}, \mathsf{inst}_{i+k}, \pi)$$
$$Inst'' = \mathsf{NIFS}.\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{Inst}', \mathsf{inst}', \pi')$$

The folding scheme ensures that these values of Inst', Inst'' are the same as the values computed in steps 6a and 6c. Then  $H_F$  computes

$$h'_0 = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{zk}, i + k, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, \mathsf{Inst}''; 0)$$

and  $h'_0$  becomes part of inst". Moreover, by construction of  $H_F$  we have that

$$h_j' = \mathsf{HCom}.\mathsf{Commit}(z_j', r_j')$$

for all  $j \in [n]$ . Therefore the check in step 2b of  $\mathcal{V}$  is satisfied.

Second, by the construction of ZK we have that  $w''.(z', \mathbf{z}') = w''.(z, \mathbf{z})$ . Furthermore, since w'' represents a tuple of satisfying wire values for  $H_F$ , we have that  $w''.z = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, w''.\mathbf{z})$ . Finally, we know that  $\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = w''.z$ . These facts imply that

$$\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathsf{w}''.\mathbf{z}')$$

This means that the check in step 2c of  $\mathcal{V}$  is satisfied.

Third, by the construction of ZK we have that

$$\mathsf{inst}''.(\overline{E},u) = (\mathsf{inst}_\perp.\overline{E},1)$$

So the check in step 2d of  $\mathcal{V}$  is satisfied.

Fourth, we already argued that  $(Inst'', W'') \in \mathcal{R}_F$  and  $(inst'', w'') \in \mathcal{R}_F$ , so the check in step 2e of  $\mathcal{V}$  is satisfied.

Fifth, putting together all the above claims, we have that

$$\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i+k, z_0, \widetilde{z_{i+k}}, \Pi_{i+k}) = 1.$$

{36}------------------------------------------------

Claim 21.  $\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = z_{i+k}$ 

*Proof.* We proved in Claim 17 that

$$\mathsf{w}_{i+k}.z' = z_{i+k}$$

Furthermore, by the construction of  $H_F$  and  $\mathsf{ZK}$ , we have that

$$\widetilde{z_{i+k}} = \mathsf{w}''.z = \mathsf{w}_{i+k}.z' = z_{i+k}$$

#### <span id="page-36-0"></span>4.5.2 Knowledge Soundness

<span id="page-36-1"></span>Lemma 22 (Knowledge Soundness). The collaborative IVC construction in Section 4.4 satisfies adaptive knowledge soundness (Definition 12).

*Proof.* Consider an arbitrary expected polynomial-time adversary  $\mathcal{P}^*$  and constant  $k \in \mathbb{N}$ . Let  $\mathsf{pp} = (\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{HCom}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . For an arbitrary random tape r, let  $(F, z_0, z, \Pi) \leftarrow \mathcal{P}^*(\mathsf{pp}, r)$  and  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{vk}) \leftarrow \mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F)$ . Suppose that

$$\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, k, z_0, z, \Pi) = 1$$

with probability  $\epsilon$  over r.

We must construct an expected polynomial-time extractor  $\mathcal{E}$  that on input (pp, r), outputs  $(\omega_0, \ldots, \omega_{k-1})$  such that by computing

$$z_i \leftarrow F(z_{i-1}, \omega_{i-1})$$

for  $i \in [k]$ , we have that  $z_k = z$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  over r.

We show inductively that we can construct an expected polynomial-time extractor  $\mathcal{E}_i(\mathsf{pp},r)$  that outputs  $((z_i,\ldots,z_{k-1}),(\omega_i,\ldots,\omega_{k-1}),F^*,\Pi_i)$  such that for all  $j\in\{i+1,\ldots,k\},\,F^*=F$ 

$$z_j = F(z_{j-1}, \omega_{j-1})$$

and

$$\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i) = 1 \tag{4.4}$$

for  $z_k = z$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Then, because in the base case when i = 0,  $\mathcal{V}$  checks that  $z_0 = z_i$ , the values  $(\omega_0, \ldots, \omega_{k-1})$  retrieved by  $\mathcal{E}(\mathsf{pp}, r) = \mathcal{E}_0(\mathsf{pp}, r)$  are such that computing  $z_{i+1} = F(z_i, \omega_i)$  for all  $i \geq 1$  gives  $z_k = z$ . At a high level, to construct an extractor  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$ , we first assume the existence of  $\mathcal{E}_i$  that satisfies the inductive hypothesis. We then use  $\mathcal{E}_i(\mathsf{pp})$  to construct an adversary for the non-interactive folding scheme, which we denote as  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$ . This in turn guarantees an extractor for the non-interactive folding scheme, which we denote as  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$ . We then use  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$  to construct  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$  that satisfies the inductive hypothesis.

In the base case, for i = k, let  $\mathcal{E}_k(\mathsf{pp}, r)$  output  $(F, \bot, \bot, \Pi_k)$  where  $(F, \Pi_k)$  is the output of  $\mathcal{P}^*(\mathsf{pp}, r)$ . By the premise,  $\mathcal{E}_k$  succeeds with probability  $\epsilon$  in expected polynomial-time.

For  $1 \leq i < k$ , suppose  $\mathcal{E}$  can construct an expected polynomial-time extractor  $\mathcal{E}_i$  that outputs  $((z_i, \ldots, z_{k-1}), (\omega_i, \ldots, \omega_{k-1}))$ , and  $F, \Pi_i$  that satisfies the inductive hypothesis. To construct an extractor  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$ , we first construct an adversary  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}$  for second non-interactive folding step in the in the zero-knowledge layer as follows:

$$\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}(\mathsf{pp},r)$$
:

- (1) Let  $((z_i, \ldots, z_{n-1}), (\omega_i, \ldots, \omega_{n-1}), F, \Pi_i) \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_i(\mathsf{pp}, r)$ .
- (2) Parse  $\Pi_i$  as ((Inst'', W''), (inst'', w'')).
- (3) Parse w" to retrieve (Inst', inst',  $\pi$ ').

{37}------------------------------------------------

(4) Output  $((Inst'', W'', \pi'), F, Inst', inst')$ 

$$\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{state},r)$$
:

- (1) Parse state as  $(Inst'', W'', \pi')$
- (2) Output (Inst", W",  $\pi$ ')

We argue that, in the case that the mode' parsed from  $\Pi_i$  is zk, we must have that  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}$  succeeds in producing an accepting folded instance-witness pair (Inst'', W''), and corresponding proof  $\pi'$  for instances (Inst', inst'), with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  in expected polynomial-time. Indeed, by the inductive hypothesis, we have that  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i) = 1$ , where  $\Pi_i \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_i(\mathsf{pp}, r)$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Therefore, by the verifier's checks we have that (inst'', w'') and (Inst'', W'') are satisfying instance-witness pairs. Moreover, given  $(\mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}, \mathbf{z}, \mathsf{mode}', \mathbf{h}')$  parsed from (inst'', w''), we have that

$$h'_0 = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', i, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, \mathsf{Inst}''; 0)$$

and for every  $j \in [n]$ 

$$h'_j = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(z_j; r_j).$$

Because V ensures that  $(inst''.\overline{E}, inst''.u) = (inst_{\perp}.\overline{E}, 1)$  we have that w'' is indeed a satisfying assignment for  $H_F$  (and not just a trivially satisfying witness). Then, by the construction of  $H_F$  and the binding property of HCom, and by assumption that  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$ , we have that

$$Inst'' = NIFS.\mathcal{V}(vk, Inst', inst', \pi')$$

with probability  $\epsilon - \text{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Then, by the knowledge soundness of the underlying non-interactive folding scheme (Definition 8) there exists an extractor  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}'_{i-1}$  that outputs satisfying witnesses  $(\mathsf{W}',\mathsf{w}')$  corresponding to the output instances (Inst', inst') of  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}(\mathsf{pp},r)$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  in expected polynomial-time.

Using  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}'_{i-1}$  (in the case where the parsed mode' is  $\mathsf{zk}$ ) we construct an adversary  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}_{i-1}$  for the non-interactive folding scheme as follows:

# $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}_{i-1}(\mathsf{pp},r)$ :

- (1) Let  $((z_i, \ldots, z_{n-1}), (\omega_i, \ldots, \omega_{n-1}), \Pi_i) \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_i(\mathsf{pp}, r)$ .
- (2) Parse  $\Pi_i$  as ((Inst'', W''), (inst'', w'')).
- (3) Parse mode' from w".
- (4) If mode' = zk:
  - (a) Parse w" to retrieve (Inst', Inst, inst,  $\pi$ ).
  - (b) Let  $(W', w') \leftarrow \widetilde{\mathcal{E}}'_{i-1}(pp, r)$
  - (c) Output (Inst, inst) and  $((Inst', W'), \pi)$ .
- (5) If mode' = increment:
  - (a) Parse w" to retrieve (Inst, inst,  $\pi$ )
  - (b) Let  $(Inst', W') \leftarrow (Inst'', W'')$
  - (c) Output (Inst, inst) and  $((Inst', W'), \pi)$ .

By a nearly identical argument as above we have that  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}_{i-1}$  succeeds in producing an accepting folded instance-witness pair (Inst', W'), for instances (Inst, inst), with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  in expected polynomial-time.

Then, by the knowledge soundness of the underlying non-interactive folding scheme there exists an extractor  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$  that outputs  $(\mathsf{W},\mathsf{w})$  such that  $(\mathsf{Inst},\mathsf{W})$  and  $(\mathsf{inst},\mathsf{w})$  satisfy  $H_F$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  in expected polynomial-time.

Given an expected polynomial-time  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}_{i-1}$  and an expected polynomial-time  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$ , we construct an intermediate expected polynomial-time  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$  that outputs either an unblinded proof  $\Pi_i$  or a potentially blinded proof  $\Pi_{i-1}$  as follows

## $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}(\mathsf{pp};r)$ :

{38}------------------------------------------------

- (1) Let  $((\mathsf{Inst},\mathsf{inst}),(\mathsf{Inst}',\mathsf{W}'),\pi)\leftarrow\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}_{i-1}(\mathsf{pp};r)$
- (2) Let  $((z_i, \ldots, z_{n-1}), (\omega_i, \ldots, \omega_{n-1}), F, \Pi_i) \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_i(\mathsf{pp}, r)$ .
- (3) Parse mode' from  $\Pi_i.w_i$ .
- (4) Let  $(\mathsf{w},\mathsf{W}) \leftarrow \widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}(\mathsf{pp},r)$ .
- (5) If mode' = zk:
  - (a) Let  $\Pi'_i \leftarrow ((\mathsf{Inst}, \mathsf{W}), (\mathsf{inst}, \mathsf{w}))$
  - (b) Output the unblinded proof of the same increment  $((z_i, \ldots, z_{n-1}), (\omega_i, \ldots, \omega_{n-1}), \Pi_i')$
- (6) If mode' = increment:
  - (a) Parse  $z_{i-1}$  and  $\omega_{i-1}$  from  $\Pi_i.w_i$ .
  - (b) Let  $\Pi_{i-1} \leftarrow ((\mathsf{Inst}, \mathsf{W}), (\mathsf{inst}, \mathsf{w}))$ .
  - (c) Output a proof of the prior increment  $((z_{i-1},\ldots,z_{n-1}),(\omega_{i-1},\ldots,\omega_{n-1}),\Pi_{i-1}).$

Given the above extractor we define another intermediate extractor  $\mathcal{E}''_{i-1}$  exactly as above but with all underlying calls to  $\mathcal{E}_i$  replaced with calls to  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$  (including in the subroutines that induce the necessary subextractors). In particular, we first construct  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'^*_{i-1}$  exactly as  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}$  but replacing the underlying call to  $\mathcal{E}_i$  with  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$ . Then, we define  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}'^*_{i-1}$  as the corresponding extractor. Next, we construct  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'^*_{i-1}$  exactly as  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}'_{i-1}$  but replacing the underlying call to  $\mathcal{E}_i$  with  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$  and replacing the underlying call to  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}'_{i-1}$  with  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}'^*_{i-1}$ . Then we let  $\mathcal{E}^*_{i-1}$  be the corresponding extractor. Finally, we define  $\mathcal{E}''_{i-1}$  exactly as  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$  except with the underlying call to  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}_{i-1}$  replaced with  $\widetilde{\mathcal{P}}^*_{i-1}$ , the underlying call to  $\mathcal{E}_i$  with  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$ , the underlying call to  $\mathcal{E}_i$  with  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$ , the underlying call to  $\mathcal{E}_i$  with  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$ .

Now the desired extractor  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$  first runs  $\mathcal{E}_i$  to get  $\Pi_i$  and parses out mode'. If mode' is increment,  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$  runs  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$ , and otherwise runs  $\mathcal{E}''_{i-1}$  to output  $((z_{i-1},\ldots,z_{n-1}),(\omega_{i-1},\ldots,\omega_{n-1}),\Pi_{i-1})$ .

We now reason about the success probability of  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$ . First, suppose that mode' is increment. We first reason that the outputs  $(z_{i-1}, \ldots, z_{n-1})$ , and  $(\omega_{i-1}, \ldots, \omega_{n-1})$  are valid. By the inductive hypothesis, we already have that for all  $j \in \{i+1, \ldots, T\}$ ,

<span id="page-38-0"></span>
$$z_j = F(z_{j-1}, \omega_{j-1}),$$

and that  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, ((\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i), (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i))) = 1$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Given  $(\mathbf{h}', \mathbf{r}', \mathbf{z}')$  parsed from  $(\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i)$ ,  $\mathcal{V}$  additionally checks that

$$\mathbf{h}_0' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', i, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_{\perp}, \mathsf{Inst}_i; 0), \tag{4.5}$$

for every  $j \in [n]$ 

$$\mathbf{h}_{j}' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathbf{z}_{j}'; \mathbf{r}_{j}') \tag{4.6}$$

and that  $z_i = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ . Then, by the construction of  $H_F$  and the binding property of HCom, we have that

<span id="page-38-1"></span>
$$F(z_{i-1}, \omega_{i-1}) = z_i$$

with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Next, we argue that  $\Pi_{i-1}$  is valid. Let  $(\mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}, \mathbf{z})$  and mode' be parsed from  $(\mathsf{inst}_{i-1}, \mathsf{w}_{i-1})$ . Because  $(\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i)$  satisfies  $H_F$ , and  $(\mathsf{Inst}_{i-1}, \mathsf{inst}_{i-1})$  were retrieved from  $\mathsf{w}_i$ , by the binding property of  $\mathsf{HCom}$ , and by Equations (4.5) and (4.6), we have that

$$\begin{aligned} \mathbf{h}_0 &= \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', i-1, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{Inst}_{i-1}; 0) \\ \mathbf{h}_j &= \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathbf{z}_j; \mathbf{r}_j) \quad \forall j \in [n] \\ (\mathsf{inst}_{i-1}.\overline{E}, \mathsf{inst}_{i-1}.u) &= (\overline{0}, 1) \\ z_{i-1} &= \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}) \end{aligned}$$

{39}------------------------------------------------

Additionally, in the case where i = 1, by the base case check of  $H_F$ , we have that  $z_{i-1} = z_0$ . Because  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$  succeeds in producing  $(\mathsf{w}_{i-1}, \mathsf{W}_{i-1})$  such that  $(\mathsf{inst}_{i-1}, \mathsf{w}_{i-1})$  and  $(\mathsf{Inst}_{i-1}, \mathsf{W}_{i-1})$  are satisfying with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we have that

$$V(vk, i-1, z_0, z_{i-1}, \Pi_{i-1}) = 1$$

with probability  $\epsilon - \text{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Now, suppose instead that  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$ . Then, it suffices to demonstrate that  $\mathcal{E}'_{i-1}$  produces a valid  $((z_i, \ldots, z_{n-1}), (\omega_i, \ldots, \omega_{n-1}), \Pi_i)$  and that the mode parsed from  $\Pi_i$  is increment. If both of these requirements hold then, by the above reasoning we will have that  $\mathcal{E}''_{i-1}$  invoked by  $\mathcal{E}_{i-1}$  will output a valid  $((z_{i-1}, \ldots, z_{n-1}), (\omega_{i-1}, \ldots, \omega_{n-1}), \Pi_{i-1})$ . As above, we already have that for all  $j \in \{i+1, \ldots, T\}$ ,

$$z_i = F(z_{i-1}, \omega_{i-1}),$$

and that  $\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, ((\mathsf{Inst}_i, \mathsf{W}_i), (\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i))) = 1$  with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Next, we will argue that  $\Pi'_i = ((\mathsf{Inst}'_i, \mathsf{W}'_i), (\mathsf{inst}'_i, \mathsf{w}'_i))$  is valid, and, when  $\Pi'_i.\mathsf{w}'_i$  is parsed, we have that  $\mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{increment}$ . Let  $(\mathbf{h}, \mathbf{r}, \mathbf{z})$  and  $\mathsf{mode}'$  be parsed from  $(\mathsf{inst}'_i, \mathsf{w}'_i)$ . Because  $(\mathsf{inst}_i, \mathsf{w}_i)$  satisfies  $H_F$ , and  $(\mathsf{Inst}'_i, \mathsf{inst}'_i)$  were retrieved from  $\mathsf{w}_i$ , by the binding property of  $\mathsf{HCom}$ , and that the verifier additionally checks that

$$\mathbf{h}_0' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}', i, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_\perp, \mathsf{Inst}_i'; 0), \tag{4.7}$$

for every  $j \in [n]$ 

$$\mathbf{h}_{i}' = \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathbf{z}_{i}'; \mathbf{r}_{i}') \tag{4.8}$$

and  $z_i = SSS.open(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}')$ . we have that

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{h}_0 &= \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathsf{vk}_{\mathsf{NIFS}}, \mathsf{mode}, i, z_0, \mathsf{inst}_\bot, \mathsf{Inst}_i; 0) \\ \mathbf{h}_j &= \mathsf{HCom.Commit}(\mathbf{z}_j; \mathbf{r}_j) \quad \forall j \in [n] \\ (\mathsf{inst}_i.\overline{E}, \mathsf{inst}_i.u) &= (\overline{0}, 1) \\ z_i &= \mathsf{SSS.open}(\mathbb{F}, \mathbf{z}) \end{split}$$

Then, because  $\widetilde{\mathcal{E}}_{i-1}$  succeeds in producing  $(w'_i, W'_i)$  such that  $(\mathsf{inst}'_i, w'_i)$  and  $(\mathsf{Inst}'_i, W'_i)$  are satisfying with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we have that

$$\mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i') = 1$$

with probability  $\epsilon - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Moreover because  $w_i$  is satisfying we must have that  $\mathsf{mode} \neq \mathsf{mode}' = \mathsf{zk}$ . Due to the binding property of HCom this  $\mathsf{mode} = \mathsf{increment}$  is precisely equal to  $\mathsf{mode}'$  parsed from  $\Pi_i'$ .

#### <span id="page-39-0"></span>4.5.3 t-Zero-Knowledge

<span id="page-39-1"></span>**Lemma 23** (t-Zero-Knowledge). Let  $t < \frac{n}{2}$ . In the collaborative IVC construction in Section 4.4, let  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  be replaced with any protocol that securely computes  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  with abort in the presence of a malicious adversary controlling  $\leq t$  parties (such as  $\pi_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  from Section 5). Then the resulting scheme satisfies t-zero-knowledge (Definition 14).

Proof. Recall that t-zero-knowledge (Definition 14) is satisfied if the wrapper protocol  $\pi_{zk}^{fg} = \pi_{zk}^{fg}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{P}, \mathcal{V}]$  securely computes the functionality  $\mathcal{F}_{zk} = \mathcal{F}_{zk}[\mathcal{K}, \mathcal{V}]$ . As it is written in Section 4.4, the protocol  $\mathcal{P}$  is constructed in the  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$ -hybrid model. First, we will prove that the protocol  $\pi_{zk}^{fg}$  securely computes  $\mathcal{F}_{zk}$  in the  $(f_{\mathcal{G}}, \mathcal{F}_{CFS})$ -hybrid model (Lemma 25). Then the modular composition theorem (Lemma 24) implies that if we replace  $\mathcal{F}_{CFS}$  with a protocol that securely computes it, then the resulting version of  $\pi_{zk}^{fg}$  still securely computes  $\mathcal{F}_{zk}$ , so t-zero-knowledge is still satisfied.

Lemma 24 below is Canneti's modular composition theorem (for the case of secure function evaluation).

<span id="page-39-2"></span>**Lemma 24 (Modular Composition, [Can00] Corollary 7).** Let t < n, let  $m \in \mathbb{N}$ , and let  $f_1, \ldots, f_m, g$  be n-party functions. Let  $\pi$  be an n-party protocol that non-adaptively t-securely evaluates g in the  $(f_1, \ldots, f_m)$ -hybrid model where no more than one ideal evaluation call is made at each round. Let  $\rho_1, \ldots, \rho_m$  be n-party protocols that non-adaptively t-securely evaluate  $f_1, \ldots, f_m$ , respectively. Then the protocol  $\pi^{\rho_1, \ldots, \rho_m}$  non-adaptively t-securely evaluates g.

{40}------------------------------------------------

For our purposes, we set m = 1, f<sup>1</sup> = FCFS, g = Fzk. Additionally, let π be the protocol πzk constructed in [Fig. 4.1](#page-20-0) that is defined in the (fG, FCFS)-hybrid model. [Lemma 25](#page-40-0) shows that π securely computes g with abort in the (fG, FCFS)-hybrid model. Then let us replace FCFS in the IVC construction with any protocol that securely computes it. Then [Lemma 24](#page-39-2) says that the resulting wrapper protocol πzk securely computes Fzk, and therefore the new IVC construction satisfies t-zero-knowledge.

It remains to prove [Lemma 25](#page-40-0) below.

<span id="page-40-0"></span>Lemma 25 (t-Zero-Knowledge in the (fG, FCFS)-Hybrid Model). πzk securely computes Fzk with abort in the (fG, FCFS)-hybrid model in the presence of a malicious adversary corrupting at most t parties in [n].

Proof.

Overview: To prove the claim, we will construct a simulator S that simulates the corrupted parties' view of πzk. S computes most of πzk [\(Fig. 4.1\)](#page-20-0) honestly, simulating the messages sent to A from the honest provers H. However, S does not know the honest parties' actual witness fragments (W<sup>j</sup> ) <sup>j</sup>∈H, so S chooses dummy values instead. At the end of step [5](#page-31-4) of P, the real-world provers have computed an unblinded, but accepting, proof that z<sup>0</sup> maps to zi+<sup>k</sup> after i + k increments. In the ideal world, S does not hold a valid proof of this fact because it used dummy values for (W<sup>j</sup> ) <sup>j</sup>∈H.

Next, S will modify their proof to be an accepting proof that z<sup>0</sup> maps to zi+k. To do so, S modifies (insti+k,wi+k), computed by the final invocation of Increment, so that (insti+k,wi+k) claims that the (i + k)-th increment outputs zi+k. For this step, S uses the trapdoor for the Pedersen commitment.

Finally, during the zero knowledge layer (step [6](#page-31-7) of P), the provers add random blinding values to sections of the proof. In the ideal world, these random values will hide the fact that S computed its proof using dummy values of (W<sup>j</sup> ) <sup>j</sup>∈H.

Let C ⊆ [n] be the set of ≤ t corrupted provers, and let A be a PPT adversary that corrupts C. It suffices to consider the case where |C| ≥ 1. Since the honest parties in πzk have no output, we just need to simulate the view of the corrupted parties. If |C| = 0, then there is no view of the corrupted parties to simulate.

Next, we describe the ideal-world simulator S that runs A internally and simulates A's real-world view.

## Simulator S:

- 1. Initialization.
  - (a) On behalf of each corrupted prover j ∈ C, S receives inputs (λ, F, i, k, z0, z<sup>i</sup> , Π<sup>i</sup> , W<sup>j</sup> ). S initializes A on all the inputs it received and runs A internally.
  - (b) Simulate pp.
    - i. Let L, M, N be the R1CS parameters of the circuit H<sup>F</sup> .
    - ii. Sample and compute

$$\begin{split} (\mathsf{pp}_E, \tau_E) &\leftarrow \mathsf{Ped}.\mathsf{TGen}(1^\lambda, M) \\ (\mathsf{pp}_W, \tau_W) &\leftarrow \mathsf{Ped}.\mathsf{TGen}(1^\lambda, N) \\ \mathsf{pp} &= (L, M, N, \mathsf{pp}_E, \mathsf{pp}_W) \end{split}$$

- iii. Send pp to A.
- <span id="page-40-1"></span>(c) Compute

$$(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{vk}) \leftarrow \mathcal{K}(\mathsf{pp}, F)$$
$$b \leftarrow \mathcal{V}(\mathsf{vk}, i, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i)$$

- (d) If b = 0 or k = 0, then skip to [step 5.](#page-41-0) Otherwise, continue.
- (e) For each honest party j ∈ H, choose their witnesses W<sup>j</sup> arbitrarily. Then set W = (W<sup>j</sup> ) j∈[n] .

{41}------------------------------------------------

2. Run steps 1 - 5 of  $\mathcal{P}$  using the simulated values of  $(\mathsf{pk}, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W)$ , except stop before the final iteration of step 5b (Increment).  $\mathcal{S}$  follows  $\mathcal{P}$  as-written and performs the steps assigned to  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  and the honest provers.  $\mathcal{S}$ 's internal simulation of  $\mathcal{A}$  runs the steps of the dishonest provers. Additionally,  $\mathcal{S}$  interacts with  $\mathcal{A}$  exactly as  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{CFS}}$  and the honest provers would interact with the dishonest provers.

For every increment  $\ell \in \{i, \ldots, i+k-2\}$ , when Increment is called in step 5b,  $\mathcal{S}$  receives from  $\mathcal{A}$  the witness fragments of the corrupted parties:  $(\omega_{\ell}^{\prime j})_{j \in \mathcal{C}}$ .

- <span id="page-41-7"></span><span id="page-41-5"></span><span id="page-41-3"></span><span id="page-41-2"></span>3. Simulate the final iteration  $(\ell = i + k - 1)$  of step 5b (Increment).
  - (a)  $\mathcal{A}$  provides inputs  $\mathbf{r}'_{\mathcal{C}}, \mathbf{z}'_{\mathcal{C}}, (\omega'^{j}_{\ell})_{\forall j \in \mathcal{C}}$ .
  - (b) Follow Increment as written for steps 1 9 to compute (inst, w).
  - (c) Compute  $z_{i+k}$ : For each  $j \in \mathcal{C}$ ,

let 
$$W'_j = \left(\omega_\ell^{\prime j}\right)_{\ell \in \{i, \dots, i+k-1\}}$$

Send to  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}$  the inputs  $(\lambda, F, i, k, z_0, z_i, \Pi_i, W'_j)$  on behalf of each party  $j \in \mathcal{C}$ . Also send a list of the corrupted parties and the input  $\mathsf{pp}$ .  $\mathcal{F}_{\mathsf{zk}}$  responds with b = 1 and  $z_{i+k}$ .
